< Text>
First off, Noble Ale Works is incredible. They have a fantastic selection of dark beers which is sadly missing at a lot of breweries. Their overall selection is also amazing.

The area itself feels more like a brewery. Inside it's a little more mature and you won't find children running around screaming like you might at other places. It's a great place to chill.

Now, the area nearby is a bit sketch. I can't say that I would go hang out or walk my alcohol off around the industrial area, but that's not any fault of theirs. Plus, that does not hamper my ability to enjoy their beer.

Overall, it's definitely worth checking out!< /Text>

<userid>114920156914327789415</userid><username>Yuhan Zhang</username>< Time>
1543558031735<//Time>
<rate>5< /rate>< text>
I am not a drinker but the atmosphere here is great. You can drink while getting a good view of the brewing process. Beer is available in 64oz (1893ml), 32oz(946ml), 16oz (473ml), 12oz (366ml) and 4oz (118ml). 15 flavours are available, including Nose Candy and Djordje. Prices range from $2 to $26 per glass. Coffee and ice tea are also available for non-drinkers. Free Wifi is one login away. You can watch ESPN here on TV or read "Beer Paper" or "Oc Weekly". Public restroom is available. Noble Ale Works merchandise, eg hoodie and glassware, are for sale.</text>

<user_name>Alizen</user_name>< Time>
1578471005680<//Time>
<Rating>4</Rating><review>Noble Ale

Whether you're a beer lover or otherwise, Noble Ale is definitely a place for everyone to visit. Located conveniently near Disneyland, Honda Center, and Angel Stadium, this place is a great spot for those who want to grab a drink without spending too much on a glass.

It was my first time coming here and finding the location is actually pretty difficult. It's tucked away inside a warehouse and if you didn't have the exact address to the brewery you really wouldn't be able to find it.

The ambiance in the brewery could be improved if their lights were dimmed a bit more. Because it's situated inside a warehouse it's got the appeal of one and personally I'd expect a little less lighting when I grab a beer. The dimmed lighting would make it an essential for those who are going on a casual date. It's a personal thing, so if lighting doesn't bother you then this place will do just fine.

Limited seating is available because it is a small brewery. You have seats at the bar and several stools around barrels that they use for tables.

I think it's great that they make their own beers here and that each one is so unique! I'm a big fan of chai tea so I ordered the "I believe I can chai" in a 12oz which cost about $6. It was great! Tasted just like chai tea with the adult elements added in ;)

I highly recommend this place and definitely plan on coming back to try their other specialties.< /review>< pictures>

MrMoruss78 Mo< /user_name>
< time>

<review>I remember coming to Noble Aleworks back in the days when it was a just a small taproom and there were only the staple beers.

The taproom is twice the size, there is ample seating, parking is great, service is fast and the staff is very atuned, but they could work on the one bathroom they have.

The beers are a step up from from what I remember being served here the past couple of years.  I think the variety is greater and Noble has ventured on more flavors.

Take for example, the Cinnamon Roast Crunch; Naughty Sauce with Saigon cinnamon swirls. 5.4% alcohol. A golden Milk Stout. Imagine drinking the the last bit of milk when done with a bowl of cinnamon toast crunch, except with smooth tasting beer. And yet another take on the naughty sauce. Bean BUMP (IMPERIAL NAUGHTY SAUCE). 12.7% alcohol. No need to say more. Just do it.  My wife is a fan of IPA'S so she went with the Big Whig. A West coast IPA that tastes drinks fast with a smooth finish.

Like I said previously, i haven't been coming here lately, but i sure am going to continue!< /review><pictures>None<//pictures><resp>None</resp><gmap_id>0x80dcd7a1e676e223:0x89836939c65ddb3</gmap_id></record>

< userid>
113897371292918169007</userid>
< name>
Ian - Fr0wnZ<//name>
<date>1408469360620< /date><Rate>5</Rate>< Review>
I am a little disappointed I didn't visit Noble Ale Works sooner. I recently came in with a friend a couple weeks ago on a mini brew hop. He mentioned Noble Ale and was very excited because this one of a few breweries which I needed to visit.

Noble stays open late, which is a plus. Fortunately, we arrived on time a little after 11pm on a Friday night. We missed the food at the previous brewery, and we just got the food truck who was packing up for the night. I didn't get the name of the food truck but the food was good. We both got two chicken bowls and then it was off inside to grab our brews.

The atmosphere of the brewery wasn't bad at all. There's two rooms, one with regular seating; bar stools, high chairs & tables, and table seating. The second room is more of standing room, but there are some seats available. Surprisingly, there wasn't a wait to grab a drink and it was cheap too. My friend & I ordered "Man's Milk" and "Mexican Lager" with both drinks coming out to $9. I had to check the receipt again wondering if I was only charged for one drink.

The bartender behind the counter was nice enough to spark a conversation and allow us to try the taste testers, ensuring we received the best beer for our tastes. He suggested a brown ale, which was delicious. I definitely will have that next time I'm there, if available. The growlers are also pretty cheap. I believe it was $10 for the growler and fill for the small. I look forward to my next visit at this brewery.</Review>

<Text>We ordered focaccia, a pesto pasta, the Marcello pizza, and tiramisù. The dessert was good, but not amazing. The rest of the food was a religious experience. The quality, flavor, and proportions of the ingredients is outstanding, as is the care with which they're prepared and served.

The menu doesn't actually say what the Marcello is, but to try describing it, it's a somewhat deconstructed pizza, served with mostly cool ingredients that aren't baked with the bread, including mozzarella, prosciutto crudo, arugula, basil, tomatoes, shaved parmesan, and a drizzle of balsamic. <Date>1618363994987</Date><rating>5< /rating>< text>
OUR HAPPY PLACE ! If you guys are lucky like us then you have a fav place not far from home where you LOVE to eat. This was our favorite local restaurant soon after it opened in nearby Encinitas 2 years ago and has remained so....though the covid lockdown has made our love affair very difficult at times. Lately things have been moving forward again so we decided to have dinner here on Saturday. I phoned around 1pm and spoke with Sarah who reserved a table for us at 5pm. I really can't believe we go to dinner so early these days because we never eat before 6pm at home but it gets way way busy from 5pm on at this very popular eatery. In fact after we parked our wheels just a few hundred feet from the restaurant and walked towards it we could see heaps of people waiting outside for a table. It's that good ! The very second we arrived at the hostess desk at 5pm lovely hostess Benedetta escorted us to a table on the covered side patio which was already packed out. Soon after we sat down Marco the new manager came by to welcome us. We spotted Vittorio one of our fav servers and very soon he was looking after us. Fresh baked Artisan Bread & Olive Oil plus Balsamic Vinegar to dip arrived at our table. And then 2 tall glasses of Sparkling Rose materialized in front of us. My wife spotted something she favored on the Specials of the Day menu....Gnocchi - White Beef Ragu with Artichokes on Top. Okay we will share that I said plus a Giuseppe Gourmet Pizza - no sauce......Mozzarella, Porcini, Spicy Salami, Calabrese, Baby Arugula and shaved Parmigiano. My wife agreed and that is exactly what we ordered when Vittorio returned. In the meantime I walked out the front ( put on my facial mask ) to take some pics of the folks dining on the sidewalk patio and the people waiting for a table. Within a very short time our dinner order arrived together courtesy of server Ivan ( our good mate ) and everything looked sensational. My wife tried the Gnocchi first while I tucked into a slice of the Giuseppe pizza. Totally mouth watering we both agreed. My wife doesn't drink alcohol so I was scoffing down both glasses of Sparkling Rose...quite nice too ! We had half our dinner boxed to go and ordered some dessert.....Mocha Chocolate Cake which tasted very delicate & very sweet. It was just great to enjoy dinner here again after so long. I said goodbye to the hard working pizza oven guys in the kitchen and lovely Sarah at the hostess desk. WE LOVE IT !< /text>

< Text>
Had a nice dinner to start the night. Between the two of us, we ordered a salad, pasta and pizza to try each thing and also shared a bottle of wine.
We got the octopus carpaccio salad. Thinly slice tentacles that was marinated in lemon juice over a bed of arugula and a few half slices grape tomatoes and olives.
The puttanesca pizza was topped with mozzarella, anchovies, capers and olives. It was salty but beautifully tasty.
For the pasta, I wanted the bucatini pasta with the Amatriciana sauce. The noodle is like a straw, and the tomato sauce was a bit smoky from the bacon. Very good!
We got there early because it is first come first serve. The staff work like a team. Quick friendly service. We got bread with lentils in EVOO and a bottle of water for our table. The staff all wore their uniform t-shirts all with a variety of cheeky slogans of “fork”. The seating is tight, but comfortable. They have a unisex restroom with fun wall art. I’ll definitely be back if I’m in town again.<//Text>

<Review>We love the restaurant in South Park, so we were really happy that they came to Encinitas. We got lucky and got seats at the "bar" (which really just overlooks part of the kitchen), so we didn't have to wait. Next time, we'll ask to sit outside, as we love the outdoor seating in South Park. The bread was warm and the lentils are a nice addition. <text>MAGNIFICO ! My wife and I had dinner here last night at this newly opened Italian restaurant. From experience knowing that Buona Forchetta locations get busy we arrived around 5 pm. A young lady greeted us at the entrance and showed us to a table in the side courtyard. It was packed out inside and half full on the patio already. A server fetched us a couple of glasses of water as we settled down to peruse the menu.I ordered the house IPA which the effervescent manager Giuseppe hand delivered to our table. A server named Liz brought us a free appetizer of fresh bread & marinated vegetable topping. We had been here 5 minutes and were feeling spoiled rotten. Our main server Luca took our dinner order for a plate of Amatriciana / Bucatini pasta & the Barbara white pizza. Giuseppe the manager came by to say hello again and check on us. In the twinkling of an eye our meals arrived at our table. Friendly server Liz popped by to grate fresh parmigiana on both our meals. And of course I added some chili flakes to my half of the fabulous looking pizza. The pasta tasted so perfect and the sauce just a tad spicy. The pizza was exactly as we used to at Buona Forchetta restaurants....a little crusty around the edge and soft near the center with that beautiful Italian flavor. We ate everything in front of us. We could have fitted in some Gelato for dessert but Giuseppe informed us they didn't have the gelato yet.....we understood as they only opened 5 days ago. We had been chatting all evening with the friendly couple at the next table...Tony & Rachel and really had a sensational evening. Sadly it was time to go and there was a throng of people on the sidewalk waiting to grab our table. We paid the bill and said goodbye to our mate Giuseppe. We will tell our friends and can't wait to come back !</text><pictures>None<//pictures>< Resp>

This is a story about a young man and his everlasting journey to acquire his drivers licence. On the morning of Wednesday October 12th a man by the name of Louis arrived at my house and took me on a journey to practice my driving skills and see how I can improve on my ability to drive a vehicle from one point to another. At first I had some discomfort with my seat but eventally got it to the right setting i was most comfortable with. Throughout this particular driving session we started to have conversations of the most interesting variety, including but not limited to our daily lives, our hobbies, family and whatever else crossed though our thoughts. I went through many trials such as the dreaded U turn, changing the lanes and most of all getting used to the stiffness of the breaks in the vehicle I was operating. Every one of these trials and tribulations I conquered with the greatest of patience and ease. Having honed my skills I hopefully get closer and closer to reaching my goal of finally obtaining a driver's license and being able to get around more efficiently. Long story short this place is great!< /text>

<pictures>None<//pictures><review>This place is fascinating. It's an outdoor museum. Apparently the guy who dreamed it up and built it randomly decided this was the center of the world and some official in France agreed. He then named the town Felicity after his wife and began building the monument and museum. It's all outdoors and it's fascinating. They even have a spiral staircase (that leads no where) that was once part of the Eiffel Tower. The real Eiffel Tower in France.
Behind the pyramid is the granite museum where facts about the world are carved in granite. Eclectic collection of facts seeking to record the whole of human history. Great stop.</review>< UserId.>

<Text>The entire Motel 6 - Harbor City staff, including the front desk, maintenance and housekeeping, were attentive, professional, efficient and prompt.   I had to stay longer than anticipated and during that time the only turn over I witnessed was the new addition of the General Manager, Rosa, with whom from a customer perspective, was very driven and professional but also personable and kind; traits that sadly lack most front of the house staff in many of the Motel 6 locations I’ve stayed over the years.  The “housecleaning” Rosa had implemented wasn’t about replacing staff and more about about the esthetics.  Like new trash cans and stand alone ashtrays for guests.  Those charges tho small to the average person certainly helped brighten the facad of that location because the hotel from the outside could definitely use a facelift.   My room was clean upon check-in, fresh towels & linens always readily avail, ice machine never out of service (often an issue w other Motel 6 locations), pet area in the back was clean and stocked w bags,  never more than 3-4 rings when calling the front desk; both from my cell and from my room and if the lobby had a line of guests, the person working made sure to acknowledge your presence; even if not able to help immediately.  I am not a guest that needs to be pampered but I do expect to be treated w respect.   Not once did I feel that I wasn’t and would recommend this location due to that fact alone.  It was nice to see that upon my departure the original staff still remained in tact.  Shout out to Rosa, Athena, Lei, Thomas, Kathy, Teresa, Lisa and Tony (the entire staff no doubt and sry I didn’t catch everyones name) for being an amazing and hard working crew that made my unexpected and frustrating longer stay one that was pleasant and welcoming.< /Text>< pics>

<Text>Don't get me wrong, the hotel itself deserves a solid 3 stars middle of the road, with the soothing sounds of cars rushing by on the freeway all night, paper thin walls that enhance even the slightest reverberation, and cigarette holes burnt into the sheets, but the service received from this hotel was the complete antithesis of customer service oriented. After booking a 2 bed for 2 nights a week in advance, with a GUARANTEE payment option used to book, my buddy and I showed up at 2 a.m. after driving we we got off of work from Arizona only to be told that they had cancelled our GUARANTEED reservation because we hadn't checked in before 6 p.m. Okay, sure, no problem. So just book me for the second night. Oh, what's that? You've already booked the room so now I have nowhere to stay? Well isn't that welcoming me with open arms at 2 a.m.

So trying to keep my cool, I asked Vivienne, the front desk attendant at the time, when the manager would be in. Vivienne told me 10:30 and I asked her to pass on to her manager that I would be in at 11 and hoped there would be a resolution for me at that time.

Come 7:30 in the morning, after not being able to fall gently into a bed and rest my weary head from travel, the blaring and alarming sound of the phone ringing shocks me awake after a solid 4 hours of sleep(Have you ever tried to fall asleep stressed and angry? It took me a while to be able to calm down.) to let me know that, oh, well, they have a room for me for that night as well. I asked if I could just come down and pay for it when I woke up, and the lady at the front assured me it would be okay to do so.

Now, I don't know about you, but at this point my faith in Motel 6 is completely shaken to the point where I don't believe she'll hold the room for me. I don't have the smallest of slivers of faith to give to this woman that, should I close my eyes to try and get rest for a big festival that day, I'll have a room waiting for me when I wake up.

If she had the room on hold for me, it would have still been there when I came in at 11. There was no reason aside from either a complete indifference to the guest experience or spite for stating I hoped there would be a resolution when I came back that I should have gotten a call that early. I wish I could remember her name, but I was half-asleep and incredulous at the total lack of customer satisfaction. I do not, nor will I ever, endorse this Motel 6.<//Text><pictures>None</pictures>< Resp>
None<//Resp>
